  //<![CDATA[
    function loadScript(url, callback) {
      var script = document.createElement("script");
      script.type = "text/javascript";
    
      if (script.readyState) {  //Internet Explorer
          script.onreadystatechange = function() {
            if (script.readyState == "loaded" ||
                    script.readyState == "complete") {
              script.onreadystatechange = null;
              callback();
            }
          };
      } else {  //Other browsers
        script.onload = function() {
          callback();
        };
      }
    
      script.src = url;
      document.getElementsByTagName("head")[0].appendChild(script);
    }
    
    function initAppleId() {
      AppleID.auth.init({
        clientId : 'com.goodreads.app', 
        scope : 'name email',
        redirectURI: 'https://www.goodreads.com/apple_users/sign_in_with_apple_web',
        state: 'apple_oauth_state_98d1101c-ef5c-4afc-b7d6-09251da1e951'
      });
    }
    
    var initializeSiwa = function() {
      var APPLE_SIGN_IN_JS_URL =  "https://appleid.cdn-apple.com/appleauth/static/jsapi/appleid/1/en_US/appleid.auth.js"
      loadScript(APPLE_SIGN_IN_JS_URL, initAppleId);
    };
    if (typeof AppleID !== "undefined") {
      initAppleId();
    } else {
      initializeSiwa();
    }

<span id="freeTextContainer2639054022901584684">Юноша становится вампиром, сверхчеловеком, одним из представителей расы, выведшей людей для прокорма как скот. И все эт</span>
  <span id="freeText2639054022901584684" style="display:none">Юноша становится вампиром, сверхчеловеком, одним из представителей расы, выведшей людей для прокорма как скот. В новой жизни ему предстоит изучить самые важные науки для понимания современного общества: гламур и дискурс, познакомиться с реальным положением вещей в мире. <br />Актуальный сюжет узнаваемой любовной линией между Рамой и Герой (Степой и Мюс, Петром и Анкой). И все это погружено в чисто пелевинский коктейль из кастанедовщины, теософии, буддизма и мухоморов. Возможно ли такое, вообще, подделать?</span>

    <div class="section firstReview">
      

<div id="review_1753110222" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1753110222" />
    <a title="Evelina | AvalinahsBooks" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/13716524-evelina-avalinahsbooks"><img alt="Evelina | AvalinahsBooks" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1592760668p2/13716524.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1753110222?book_show_action=true">Sep 27, 2016</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Evelina | AvalinahsBooks" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Evelina | AvalinahsBooks" href="/user/show/13716524-evelina-avalinahsbooks">Evelina | AvalinahsBooks</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9781473213074" href="/book/show/29243703-empire-v">review of another edition</a>


          <div>
    <span class="greyText">Recommended to Evelina | AvalinahsBooks by: </span>
      <a href="/user/show/22928866-aist-ri">Aistė Ri</a>
  </div>


    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1753110222" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer8791949042348968297">I'll start the review a little differently this time - just for the sake of novelty (I promise there's a serious review at the bottom :D)<br/><br/>So vampires are:<br/><br/><img src='https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1475010255i/20669748.jpg' width='300' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/><br/>And for those of you who haven't seen Stargate SG-1 and thus aren't privy to the meme:<br/><br/><img src='https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1417688181ra/12490267.gif' width='300' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/><br/>But more seriously.<br/><br/>This was my introduction to Pelevin. Now I know I am going to read more of his work. For those in my friends list who are strictly English speaking - I don't know if this has been published in English yet. Might be published, but could be har</span>
  <span id="freeText8791949042348968297" style="display:none">I'll start the review a little differently this time - just for the sake of novelty (I promise there's a serious review at the bottom :D)<br><br>So vampires are:<br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1475010255i/20669748.jpg" width="300" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>And for those of you who haven't seen Stargate SG-1 and thus aren't privy to the meme:<br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1417688181ra/12490267.gif" width="300" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>But more seriously.<br><br>This was my introduction to Pelevin. Now I know I am going to read more of his work. For those in my friends list who are strictly English speaking - I don't know if this has been published in English yet. Might be published, but could be hard to obtain. Either way, my advice is - wait till it is published / find it and read it! As for Lithuanians and Russians - well, you guys have zero excuses here. Just get to it already.<br><br>This book explores a different understanding of vampires than we are used to. So not to spoil it for you, I will not elaborate. But Pelevin talks a great deal about how society is built, and in a way, it reminds me of <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/214579.The_Story_of_B_An_Adventure_of_the_Mind_and_Spirit" title="The Story of B An Adventure of the Mind and Spirit by Daniel Quinn" rel="nofollow noopener">The Story of B: An Adventure of the Mind and Spirit</a>, although that deals with it from an altogether different angle.<br>The two main characters - Rama and Hera (yes, all vampires are given god names here) are juxtaposed to represent complete naivete (Rama) and complete cynicism (or complete, intrinsic knowledge - Hera). The juxtaposition of these two allows to show the understanding of the world in the book's universe, a sort of philosophy veiled in fiction (a thing I have heard about Pelevin's works before). Pelevin challenges the very structure of society, the rot at its core. What is real freedom? If the ones who are 'free', who are on the top, still end up being pushed around, led by the hand? Is there such a thing as freedom then?<br>And the funny thing about it is, although the book depicts the world in a nihilistic, painful, although accurate and valid way, somehow, around and through and over it all, it manages to reach the meaning of life through the other side - through cynicism and lack of thereof, through nothingness. What I find quite interesting is that Pelevin managed to come to almost the same description of it as many spiritual literature works (especially of the oriental kind), but using a completely different path.<br><br>My own take is that the author tries to show a contrast of the meaning of life and how we try to reach it in broken, completely messed up ways. It's not that he preaches - he doesn't at all, but somehow it comes across as the contrasting of these two things. But that's only my take. It's written quite freely and you can take from it what you want. And I'd be curious about what some friends of mine would bring back from it.</span>
  <a data-text-id="8791949042348968297" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

<div id="review_1582781316" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1582781316" />
    <a title="Brendan" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/17999985-brendan"><img alt="Brendan" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1562070914p2/17999985.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1582781316?book_show_action=true">Mar 17, 2016</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Brendan" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Brendan" href="/user/show/17999985-brendan">Brendan</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9781473213074" href="/book/show/29243703-empire-v">review of another edition</a>


        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1582781316" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer17013722876150662893">I'll be the first to admit that taking a break from a book is never a good sign, I have been putting this off for a few weeks but the dreaded week to go before the library breaks down my door, finally came into play. This book has a lot of mythology building which I liked and found it to be fascinating when it explored the vampire lore. The characters were the biggest problem I found and with all the interesting concepts e.g. the tongue, I found the pacing lacking when it should of been engrossi</span>
  <span id="freeText17013722876150662893" style="display:none">I'll be the first to admit that taking a break from a book is never a good sign, I have been putting this off for a few weeks but the dreaded week to go before the library breaks down my door, finally came into play. This book has a lot of mythology building which I liked and found it to be fascinating when it explored the vampire lore. The characters were the biggest problem I found and with all the interesting concepts e.g. the tongue, I found the pacing lacking when it should of been engrossing. The tone was super dull and never really changed for the duration, you are always stuck in the learning part and when the red ceremony came about I found that I had drifted a little and missed a certain chunk. <br />The book probably deserves a 3.5 but definitely not a 4 so that is why I have it in the average section of my review. I don't know if I'll read the next book when it is translated to English as I'll move along to something different soon enough. Victor Pelevin may have a core audience that devours this constant tone of melodrama but I found myself wanting more, some of the most interesting characters are the supports and I didn't get much from them. The ending was decent and gave the characters an arc that would be of interest to me for that second novel but I won't be rushing out for it. <br />Literature is an interesting thing and if you don't click with the book it's hard to invest. I don't review less then three because of that fact, just because I missed it doesn't mean it's lacking. I'm definitely on the fence with this review. </span>
  <a data-text-id="17013722876150662893" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  <span id="freeText2183557654591708754" style="display:none">A great read! Endlessly charming, at times confusing Pelevin takes on all the basic social constructs and rips them apart so we can see their bowels. Consumerism, capitalism, philosophy, fashion - you name it - as we read the novel it's all demasked and served (or so it should be) on a golden platter for a young, freshly-became vampire. At times confusing narrative inside the story comes as a result of Pelevin's wish to engage with and explain the core of mind and reality itself - a concept so huge that a simple mind like mine could not hope to grasp it - yet he surpasses the hurdles with a gleaming success.</span>

<div id="review_2134268310" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2134268310" />
    <a title="Ari" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/9342957-ari"><img alt="Ari" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1336412865p2/9342957.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2134268310?book_show_action=true">Oct 15, 2017</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Ari" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Ari" href="/user/show/9342957-ari">Ari</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Hardcover 9789513145262" href="/book/show/11684413-viides-maailmanvalta">review of another edition</a>


        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2134268310" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer7940252579333653927">Not just one more vampire story - but completely different from others.<br/><br/>Of cource this wasn't a vampire story but a portrayal of Russia around year 2000. Quite critical (and satirical) I would say. <br/>Following the footsteps of Mihail Bulgakov's "The Master and Margarita" which in my opinion is definitely better (one of the best novels I've ever read). Naturally Bulgakov's novel was also very daring when published in the totalitarian Soviet Union. Pelevin should be more safe with his satire and will</span>
  <span id="freeText7940252579333653927" style="display:none">Not just one more vampire story - but completely different from others.<br /><br />Of cource this wasn't a vampire story but a portrayal of Russia around year 2000. Quite critical (and satirical) I would say. <br />Following the footsteps of Mihail Bulgakov's "The Master and Margarita" which in my opinion is definitely better (one of the best novels I've ever read). Naturally Bulgakov's novel was also very daring when published in the totalitarian Soviet Union. Pelevin should be more safe with his satire and will not be facing an evident threat to be sent to a kulag for rehabilitation. But who can say when it comes to Russia nowadays...<br /><br />Clearly one should be a Russian living in Russia to get the most out of this novel and to understand all the hints. The references to people and organisations were partly strange and unknown to me - and obviously there was a real life counterpart for most of the characters. The Finnish translator had made a good contribution by adding some information as an appendix at the end of the book. It was helpful, informative and clarified a lot. Not just trivia as she too modestly described it.<br /><br />I have earlier read "Amon Ra" from Pelevin. It was also satirical story about Russian Space program. As far as I remember, it was funnier and less difficult and demanding to comprehend.<br /><br />Both are definitely worth reading.<br /><br />Viides maailmanvalta (Empire V)<br />Tammi 2009<br /><br /><br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="7940252579333653927" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

<div id="review_2212421517" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2212421517" />
    <a title="Marc Nash" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/5136053-marc-nash"><img alt="Marc Nash" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1442559977p2/5136053.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2212421517?book_show_action=true">Dec 12, 2017</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Marc Nash" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Marc Nash" href="/user/show/5136053-marc-nash">Marc Nash</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9781473213081" href="/book/show/30364217-empire-v">review of another edition</a>


        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2212421517" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer11057367426681090870">There are so many inventive ideas on show here, but this is not a novel. It is character after character interrogating or being interrogated by one another, as two neophyte vampires gain instruction into the vampire life and by extension the humans which vampires feed and the nature of god and existence itself. <br/><br/>It's just Pelevin lecturing us, (fascinating as these ideas are) and as such was a real trial to get through. <br/><br/>So interesting meditations on existence, theology, matter, illusion and withe</span>
  <span id="freeText11057367426681090870" style="display:none">There are so many inventive ideas on show here, but this is not a novel. It is character after character interrogating or being interrogated by one another, as two neophyte vampires gain instruction into the vampire life and by extension the humans which vampires feed and the nature of god and existence itself. <br /><br />It's just Pelevin lecturing us, (fascinating as these ideas are) and as such was a real trial to get through. <br /><br />So interesting meditations on existence, theology, matter, illusion and withering attacks on fashion, advertising, politics, the Davos elite, literature and particularly the nature of money. I credit this is Pelevin not world building as such, but structuring a philosophical argument in line with Buddhist beliefs on existence and its illusory nature in order to attain true enlightenment, which he has thrown into this, a literary form of expression. It's Pelevin talking to himself, with the schizoid split of Pelevin the writer/artist and Pelevin the follower of Buddhist belief. This reads like Pelevin trying to unpick the abstruse for himself, rather than for us his readers, because he has made minimal effort to work the material for readers to absorb since this is not structured as a novel with a narrative. Ultimately, the theories seem to come down to a version of phenomenalism, hardly revolutionary.</span>
  <a data-text-id="11057367426681090870" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_3515643606" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/3515643606" />
    <a title="Nadya" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/120107823-nadya"><img alt="Nadya" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1599407763p2/120107823.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/3515643606?book_show_action=true">Sep 18, 2020</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Nadya" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Nadya" href="/user/show/120107823-nadya">Nadya</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="did not like it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">did not like it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer3515643606" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer962970120901059298">If you love propaganda, two-dimensional characters, plot holes, stiff dialogues, and ambiguous endings this book is right up your alley.<br/><br/>About ninety percent of the book Pelevin spends straight-up lecturing his readers. When I say lecturing, I mean it literally. Throughout the whole novel the main character, Rama, either a) sits in the classroom with a professor, b) does vampiery things with his fellow vampires, c) hangs out with his girlfriend-to-be. All of these characters have the same style o</span>
  <span id="freeText962970120901059298" style="display:none">If you love propaganda, two-dimensional characters, plot holes, stiff dialogues, and ambiguous endings this book is right up your alley.<br /><br />About ninety percent of the book Pelevin spends straight-up lecturing his readers. When I say lecturing, I mean it literally. Throughout the whole novel the main character, Rama, either a) sits in the classroom with a professor, b) does vampiery things with his fellow vampires, c) hangs out with his girlfriend-to-be. All of these characters have the same style of dialogue, the same demeanor and all of them lecture Rama on the history of vampires, their philosophy, and purpose. Most of the dialogues have no purpose whatsoever. Considering that Empire V is over 400 pages, it’s exhausting to remember all the fictional vampire theories only to find out that they play no role in the storyline.<br /><br />From my understanding, this book attempts to portray Russia around the year 2000. I saw no depth in Pelevin's mockery of society: he merely follows overused and annoying CONSUMERISM = BAD and CAPITALISM = EVIL tropes. <br /><br />Upon wading through the word debris, Empire V can be perceived as a meditation on existence, theology, fashion influence, advertising, politics, art, literature, and the nature of money. Although these are always interesting topics for contemplation, the tone in which they were presented is dull and never changes throughout the novel. <br /><br />Perhaps the most annoying aspect of Empire V is that all vampires are like-minded. It’s uncanny. All of them, even the main character, follow the same philosophy, have the same values, goals, desires, and even jokes. They all nurture Pelevin’s ideas without ever challenging them. The book has only one conflict, and even that, is just a romance-driven one. I felt brainwashed. <br /><br />In my opinion, Pelevin neglected the world-building and made minimal effort to help readers absorb the material. The book is structured like a gigantic, incoherent university lecture given by a professor in the midst of an existential crisis. Ultimately, the Empire V theories seem to come down to a version of phenomenalism, which is hardly revolutionary.<br /><br />TLDR. This book is pretentious and overly complicated.. Read Carlos Castaneda if you want to get the same philosophy but in a more concise and logical format.</span>
  <a data-text-id="962970120901059298" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>


      <div class="reviewFooter uitext buttons">

<div id="review_2145669808" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2145669808" />
    <a title="Jenn Morgans" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/9000137-jenn-morgans"><img alt="Jenn Morgans" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1544640846p2/9000137.jpg" /></a>

<div id="review_1911327508" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1911327508" />
    <a title="Caroline Mersey" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/17722556-caroline-mersey"><img alt="Caroline Mersey" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1361569008p2/17722556.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1911327508?book_show_action=true">Feb 12, 2017</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Caroline Mersey" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Caroline Mersey" href="/user/show/17722556-caroline-mersey">Caroline Mersey</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/17722556-caroline-mersey?shelf=review-copies">review-copies</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1911327508" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer10332036855205403821">Victor Pelevin's Empire V (English translation published by Gollancz, review copy from NetGalley) aspires to be a 21st Century The Master and Margarita. It follows a young man called Ram, who is drifting through life in modern Russia. He follows chalk marks on the floor to an apartment where he is offered a bright future. He is transformed into the vampire Rama, and is gradually educated about vampires and the controlling role they play in the world economy.<br/><br/>Pelevin paints a harsh and nihilistic </span>
  <span id="freeText10332036855205403821" style="display:none">Victor Pelevin's Empire V (English translation published by Gollancz, review copy from NetGalley) aspires to be a 21st Century The Master and Margarita. It follows a young man called Ram, who is drifting through life in modern Russia. He follows chalk marks on the floor to an apartment where he is offered a bright future. He is transformed into the vampire Rama, and is gradually educated about vampires and the controlling role they play in the world economy.<br /><br />Pelevin paints a harsh and nihilistic view of contemporary Russian society. It's a very cynical view of commercialisation: the vampires are a literal parasitic class exploiting the labour and hopes and dreams of ordinary people. They are not productive in themselves, but instead create a culture of discontent, ambition and greed that fuels the economic activity that creates the conditions for the vampires to thrive. Strange rituals link the vampires to a secret society of the rich and powerful in society, as if the Bilderberg group were participating in scenes from Stanley Kubrick's film Eyes Wide Shut. The theatre the vampires create preserves their position of dominance.<br /><br />The reader follows the naive Rama as he learns more about the new world and society he finds himself in. Like the worst social climbers out of water, he over-compensates in order to convince that he belongs as a member of the group. Pelevin contrasts Rama with another new vampire, the worldly-wise Hera. Achingly cool and very well-informed, Hera navigates vampire society with an ease and facility that Rama envies. Although regularly humiliated by her, it only fuels his attraction and desperation to please and impress her: a microcosm of vampire society's control over the rest of the world.<br /><br />Empire V is a cynical and disturbing read, but thought-provoking.</span>
  <a data-text-id="10332036855205403821" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

              <span id="reviewTextContainer874299724" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer12519168577478125864">A book about a new vampire being taught on what it is to be one. Yes, I know this sentence may turn many off. But I promise it is not Twilight. Nor is it really about vampires.<br/><br/>Just like all Pelevin books it is a philosophical satire about the society in modern Russia. Also could be applied to the rest of the world. Vampires represent the ones who control this society and we learn about the methods they use to manipulate people, glamour and discourse. Written with a very fresh style, with referen</span>
  <span id="freeText12519168577478125864" style="display:none">A book about a new vampire being taught on what it is to be one. Yes, I know this sentence may turn many off. But I promise it is not Twilight. Nor is it really about vampires.<br /><br />Just like all Pelevin books it is a philosophical satire about the society in modern Russia. Also could be applied to the rest of the world. Vampires represent the ones who control this society and we learn about the methods they use to manipulate people, glamour and discourse. Written with a very fresh style, with references to culture and events and with many moments that make one laugh and even more important think. <br /><br />I have a small issue with Pelevin's books. It seems like he keeps on writing the same book just putting the idea into a different plot and using new metaphors. Many ideas in this book were already in Generation P, which I liked more than this one (even though I rated them equally).<br /><br />There are many parts of the book where I was very much into it without wanting to put it down. But there were a few where I wished he would finally wrap it up. My favorite were the chapters about glamour and discourse as well as the final message in the book.<br /><br />As I said I liked Generation more, the reason I rated it the same is because I still really liked the book. And while some parts of it felt like a repetition of the previous work, I enjoy the uniqueness of his work compared to other books out there.</span>

<span id="freeTextContainer4536175283188042603">This must have been a difficult book to translate from the Russian to English (which was the form I read), and maybe that made for a difficult read too. I am sure that some of the context was hard, if not impossible to translate.<br/>A Westerner may also find the Russian mind set, environment and politics hard to interpret too.<br/>I would recommend anyone read "The Master and Margarita " by Mikhail Bulgakov first to get into the feel first.<br/>This book was so full of philosophical theory that a copy of "dum</span>
  <span id="freeText4536175283188042603" style="display:none">This must have been a difficult book to translate from the Russian to English (which was the form I read), and maybe that made for a difficult read too. I am sure that some of the context was hard, if not impossible to translate.<br />A Westerner may also find the Russian mind set, environment and politics hard to interpret too.<br />I would recommend anyone read "The Master and Margarita " by Mikhail Bulgakov first to get into the feel first.<br />This book was so full of philosophical theory that a copy of "dummies guide to philosophy" would not go astray either. Add a thesaurus a, a Russian-English dictionary and access to Google and/or Wikipedia and you'd be set.<br />If this gets your attention I would highly recommend Doris Lessing's Shikasta series. Just as Lessing discusses Rhetoric, Victor Pelevin asserts that Discourse and Glamour are guiding forces for society resulting in the perpetual desire for material wealth and personal kudos.<br />This and the existential questions of God and the reason for everything read independently of the plot-line. In fact the story could just as easily been told entirely separately from the philosophical contemplations.<br />There were surreal aspects of this story that made me wish it was a graphic novel, a form that I believe that it would lend itself very well to.<br />I found this to have been a challenging, but ultimately a rewarding book..</span>

<span id="freeTextContainer7910198251098583">Forget everything you’ve been told about vampires – it’s an elaborate ruse, and you’re about to discover the truth. Empire V isn’t your typical vampire novel; it throws those traditional myths completely out of the window. All you need to do is step away from the crowd, and follow those arrows painted on the street.<br /><br />Roman has his world, literally, turned upside-down as he hangs, feet strapped, to some parallel bars. Follow him as he becomes Rama, through his degustation of masterclasses in what it is to be a vampire and finds the truth about humanity.empire v<br /><br />Pelevin marvellously blends his characters with his ideology on society; from cults to politics and even banking, he dissects them exposing their corruption in such a way that will have you opening your mind and questioning what is really going on.<br /><br />From the outset, you’ll be fixated, and wishing you could join the other vampires to shape society – and you won’t even have to wait until the summer solstice.</span>

        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1889266397" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer11388623412742711211">This is the first novel I've finished in quite a while, and it was I retesting but maybe not the best choice. There are a lot of interesting ideas--Pelevin basically builds a comprehensive philosophical system built around the idea of vampirism and capitalism, which extends from philosophy, through all of society, and into cosmology. all very interesting stuff, genuinely pretty smart and also intellectually fresh. <br/><br/>But as a novel it's a huge fail. I've read a few novels of Peleivin's before but I</span>
  <span id="freeText11388623412742711211" style="display:none">This is the first novel I've finished in quite a while, and it was I retesting but maybe not the best choice. There are a lot of interesting ideas--Pelevin basically builds a comprehensive philosophical system built around the idea of vampirism and capitalism, which extends from philosophy, through all of society, and into cosmology. all very interesting stuff, genuinely pretty smart and also intellectually fresh. <br /><br />But as a novel it's a huge fail. I've read a few novels of Peleivin's before but I don't remember him being this flat a writer--the whole thing is essentially a long series of philosophical dialogues, and in the rare sections where character or narrative become important they're done pretty weakly. That would be fine I suppose if there hadn't been such potential here, but I really think peleivin had it and didn't do anything with it. There were moments where I was impressed or interested but never ones where I felt anything.</span>
  <a data-text-id="11388623412742711211" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<span id="freeTextContainer13414640240162998114">Well, it's not my favorite Pelevin book. But may be it's because I am reading a couple of his books all in a raw. I like the concepts he brings up. But the way he presents them is not the best. The concepts and ideas are very densely packed together with no story going on. <br/><br/>When you start reading Pelevin's books you immediately realize that it's like a text book in philosophy. Instead of writing plot and a story that will bring out some philosophical idea. He just makes his character talk and thi</span>
  <span id="freeText13414640240162998114" style="display:none">Well, it's not my favorite Pelevin book. But may be it's because I am reading a couple of his books all in a raw. I like the concepts he brings up. But the way he presents them is not the best. The concepts and ideas are very densely packed together with no story going on. <br /><br />When you start reading Pelevin's books you immediately realize that it's like a text book in philosophy. Instead of writing plot and a story that will bring out some philosophical idea. He just makes his character talk and think with, long, complicated philosophical tirades. Yes, they are interesting, yes I agree with slot of them. But the way they are presented to me makes me think of school lectures.<br /><br />Pelevin reminds me of Dostoevsky. But Dostoevsky had about 30% of those tirades and 70% of solid good story telling.<br /><br />I think this book is great to read in between some lighter reading.</span>
  <a data-text-id="13414640240162998114" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

  <span id="freeText4655828991729288455" style="display:none">The novel has many sides. One can consider it science fiction: parasites (or rather, symbiants) supplementing humans to form a new species; urban fantasy is also a label that fits – vampires walking among us. And given the copious amount of philosophical ramblings, "philosophical fiction" seems like a good match. But neither the fresh, original ideas, nor Pelevin's unique in-your-face writing style can make up for the patches of unmitigated, excruciatingly boring narration. One of the author's weaker works.<br /><br />Favorite quote:<br /><br />....In the 21st century, "industrial exemption" means that you don't care what does the captain of the galley where you're chained to an oar think about your jacket. Everything else is work clothes, even if you're wearing a Rolex. In fact, particularly if you're wearing a Rolex.</span>

      var newTip = new Tip($('bookCover_3278360'), "\n\n  <h2><a class=\"readable bookTitle\" href=\"https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/3278360?from_choice=false&amp;from_home_module=false\">Географ глобус пропил<\/a><\/h2>\n\n      <div>\n        by <a class=\"authorName\" href=\"/author/show/13818427._?a=9&amp;origin=related_works\">Алексей Иванов<\/a>\n      <\/div>\n\n          <div class=\"smallText uitext darkGreyText\">\n            <span class=\"minirating\"><span class=\"stars staticStars notranslate\"><span size=\"12x12\" class=\"staticStar p10\"><\/span><span size=\"12x12\" class=\"staticStar p10\"><\/span><span size=\"12x12\" class=\"staticStar p10\"><\/span><span size=\"12x12\" class=\"staticStar p10\"><\/span><span size=\"12x12\" class=\"staticStar p3\"><\/span><\/span> 4.03 avg rating &mdash; 2,055 ratings<\/span>            &mdash; published 2005\n          <\/div>\n\n    <div class=\"addBookTipDescription\">\n      \n<span id=\"freeTextContainer10055511611461285721\">Внешне сюжет книги несложен. Молодой биолог Виктор Служкин от безденежья идет работать учителем географии в обычную пермскую школу. Он борется, а потом и дружит с учениками, конфликтует с завучем, ведет девятиклассников в поход - сплавляться по реке.<\/span>\n  <span id=\"freeText10055511611461285721\" style=\"display:none\">Внешне сюжет книги несложен. Молодой биолог Виктор Служкин от безденежья идет работать учителем географии в обычную пермскую школу. Он борется, а потом и дружит с учениками, конфликтует с завучем, ведет девятиклассников в поход - сплавляться по реке. Еще он пьет с друзьями вино, пытается ужиться с женой и водит в детский сад маленькую дочку. Он просто живет… Но эту простую частную историю Алексей Иванов написал так отчаянно, так нежно и так пронзительно, что &quot;Географ глобус пропил&quot;, как это бывает с замечательными книгами, стал историей про каждого. Каждого, кто хоть однажды запутывался, терялся в жизни. Каждого, кто иногда ощущал себя таким же бесконечно одиноким, как Виктор Служкин. Каждого, кто, несмотря на одиночество и тоску, никогда не терял способность чувствовать и любить.\nРоман впервые публикуется в авторской редакции.\nВ ближайшее время по роману &quot;Географ глобус пропил&quot; будет снят четырехсерийный телесериал.\n\nИванов сочинил замечательный роман про жизнь… В &quot;Географе&quot; считывается простая и очевидная мораль: оставайся человеком и будь что будет. Иванов сочинил конструкцию настолько прочную, что она выдерживает такое давление, при котором слова про любовь к людям не кажутся ни фальшивыми, ни нелепыми.\n\n&quot;Афиша&quot;\n\n\nО действительно чудесном, что затмевает бытовую серость и все тяготы и невзгоды, этот роман. …&quot;Географ глобус пропил&quot; - обязательное чтение в программе современной литературы.\n\nlitwomen.ru\n\n\nПлохие книги пишутся для всех, хорошие для немногих. Алексей Иванов, молодой музейный работник из Перми, сумел написать замечательную книгу для многих. Это очень смешная и бесконечно печальная книга. And so begins another day in the life of an oprichnik, one of the czar’s most trusted courtiers—and one of the country’s most feared men.Welcome to the new New Russia, where futuristic technology and the draconian codes of Ivan the Terrible are in perfect synergy. Corporal punishment is back, as is a divine monarch, but these days everyone gets information from high-tech news bubbles, and the elite get high on hallucinogenic, genetically modified fish.Over the course of one day, Andrei Komiaga will bear witness to—and participate in—brutal executions; extravagant parties; meetings with ballerinas, soothsayers, and even the czarina. He will rape and pillage, and he will be moved to tears by the sweetly sung songs of his homeland. He will consume an arsenal of drugs and denounce threats to his great nation’s morals. And he will fall in love—perhaps even with a number of his colleagues.Vladimir Sorokin, the man described by Keith Gessen (in The New York Review of Books) as “[the] only real prose writer, and resident genius” of late-Soviet fiction, has imagined a near future both too disturbing to contemplate and too realistic to dismiss. But like all of his best work, Sorokin’s new novel explodes with invention and dark humor. A startling, relentless portrait of a troubled and troubling empire, Day of the Oprichnik is at once a richly imagined vision of the future and a razor-sharp diagnosis of a country in crisis.<\/span>\n  <a data-text-id=\"10452711462514577121\" href=\"#\" onclick=\"swapContent(\$(this));; return false;\">...more<\/a>\n\n    <\/div>\n\n      <div class=\'wtrButtonContainer <div class='bookAuthorProfile__about'>

<span id="freeTextContainer13195664859536765987">Victor Olegovich Pelevin is a Russian fiction writer. His books usually carry the outward conventions of the science fiction genre, but are used to construct involved, multi-layered postmodernist texts, fusing together elements of pop culture and esoteric philosophies. Some critics relate his prose to the New Sincerity and New Realism literary movements.<br/><br/>RU: <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/15016012.______________' title='Виктор Пелевин' rel='nofollow noopener'>Виктор Пелевин</a></span>
  <span id="freeText13195664859536765987" style="display:none">Victor Olegovich Pelevin is a Russian fiction writer. His books usually carry the outward conventions of the science fiction genre, but are used to construct involved, multi-layered postmodernist texts, fusing together elements of pop culture and esoteric philosophies. Some critics relate his prose to the New Sincerity and New Realism literary movements.<br /><br />RU: <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/15016012.______________" title="Виктор Пелевин" rel="nofollow noopener">Виктор Пелевин</a></span>

          <div class="stacked" tyle="padding-bottom:15px">
            <span class="readable">&ldquo;Человек думает, что добывает деньги для себя. Но в действительности он добывает их из себя. Жизнь устроена так, что он может получить немного денег в личное пользование только в том случае, если произведет значительно больше для кого-то другого. А все, что он добывает для себя, имеет свойство странным образом просачиваться между пальцев" … (.....) "Причина, по которой люди не понимают природу денег, проста, - О них разрешается говорить только в рамках карго-дискурса. Речь идет не о том, что жизнь человека перерабатывается в непонятную субстанцию, а о том, какая валюта перспективней – евро или юань. Серьезные люди о другом не говорят и не думают."<br />"– Естественно, – сказал я. – Человек стремится к деньгам, потому что иначе он умрет с голоду. Так уж жизнь устроена.<br /><br />– Слова правильные, – согласился Энлиль. – Но я бы чуть поменял их порядок. Тогда изменится акцент.<br /><br />– А как надо?<br /><br />– Жизнь устроена таким образом, что человек умрет с голоду, если станет стремиться к чему-то кроме денег. &rdquo;</span>
            <nobr>
              &mdash;
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/quotes/274045">5 likes</a>
            </nobr>
            <div class="clear"></div>
          </div>
